    [Original] Instagram and YouTube owners built 'addiction machines', trial hears
    A landmark six-week trial began in Los Angeles Superior Court as plaintiffs allege that Meta (parent of Instagram) and YouTube engineered addictive platforms that harmed minorsâ€™ mental health. In his opening statement, attorney Mark Lanier argued that the companies deliberately designed â€œaddiction machinesâ€ targeting children, citing internal documents and a 2015 email from Meta CEO Mark Zuckerberg demanding a 12% increase in user time spent on platforms. Lanier emphasized that Meta and YouTube failed to warn users of the risks, with YouTube allegedly prioritizing young users to charge advertisers more and exploit parents seeking a â€œdigital babysitting service.â€ He displayed childrenâ€™s blocks labeled â€œAddicting,â€ â€œBrains,â€ and â€œChildrenâ€ to underscore his claim that the companies manipulated young usersâ€™ brains for profit. Metaâ€™s attorney, Paul Schmidt, countered that K.G.M.â€”a minor whose case is being heard under her initialsâ€”suffered from pre-existing trauma, including family neglect, physical and verbal abuse, and bullying. He cited records showing she began therapy at age three and shared her own statements, including that her mother screamed at her and called her â€œstupid,â€ leading her to contemplate suicide. Schmidt urged the jury to consider these factors as the primary cause of her distress, not social media use. The trial, which will feature testimony from Zuckerberg, Instagram head Adam Mosseri, YouTube CEO Neal Mohan, and former Meta whistleblowers, may set a precedent for thousands of similar cases. State attorneys general, including 29 in a separate federal case, have demanded an injunction forcing Meta to delete all under-13 accounts, erase data collected on minors, and disable addictive features like infinite scroll and autoplay. They also seek time restrictions for teens and the removal of beauty-enhancing filters. Metaâ€™s recent teen account features, such as content filters for users under 16, were dismissed by prosecutors as â€œpublic relations measuresâ€ offering minimal protection. The trial drew about 100 observers, including parents who believe their children died due to platform design. Snapchat and TikTok settled with K.G.M. last month and are no longer defendants. The companies maintain they are not liable for third-party content under federal law. The outcome could significantly influence future litigation and regulatory action across the U.S.

    [Original] Romeo Is a Dead Man review â€“ a misfire from a storied gaming provocateur
    Suda51â€™s long-awaited return to original game development, *Romeo Is a Dead Man*, delivers a chaotic, incoherent experience that fails to live up to the visionary legacy of his past works. Released on PlayStation 5 (tested), Xbox, and PC via Grasshopper Manufacture and Marvelous Inc., the game follows Romeo Stargazer, a â€œdeadmanâ€ resurrected by his eccentric grandfather after being eaten by a zombie. Armed with a legally distinct lightsabre, Romeo joins the FBIâ€™s space-time police to combat interstellar criminals and endless waves of zombiesâ€”referred to as â€œbastardsâ€â€”in a narrative that remains stubbornly opaque throughout its 20-hour runtime. The gameâ€™s story, influenced by *Rick and Morty* according to Suda, is described by the developer as a love letter to â€œchicken katsuâ€ and a rebellion against â€œthe bastards,â€ yet it offers no discernible coherence. Juliet, a recurring figure who appears in dream sequences rendered in PS2-era 3D, eventually becomes a boss in the final levelâ€”adding to the gameâ€™s surreal, disjointed tone. While the core gameplayâ€”hacking and slashing zombiesâ€”initially recalls the stylish, over-the-top action of *No More Heroes*, the experience deteriorates as the game progresses. On a PS5 Pro, frame rates frequently drop to a crawl during enemy onslaughts, rendering late-game combat nearly unplayable. Visually, the game is a patchwork of styles: animated cutscenes, 16-bit pixel art in the hub world (a retro-futuristic FBI spaceship), and jagged PS2-era polygons. The hub features quirky characters like a Roman god, a talking cat, and a Jamaican journalist, with players able to buy upgrades, play mini-games, and nurture plants tied to defeated zombies. Despite its eclectic aesthetic, the final product feels less like a deliberate artistic statement and more like a childâ€™s toybox scattered across a screen. While the gameâ€™s absurdity and anti-establishment spirit may appeal to diehard fans seeking irony, it lacks the focused energy of *No More Heroes*, where simplicity served the action. Instead, *Romeo Is a Dead Man* sprawls aimlessly, failing to cohere into a meaningful or satisfying whole. It is a misfire from a once-revolutionary creator, offering fleeting moments of visual interest but ultimately falling short of its ambitions. The game releases on February 11 for $49.99.

    [Original] A.I. Personalizes the Internet but Takes Away Control
    The integration of artificial intelligence into mainstream apps is reshaping the internet, raising concerns about user control and the future of digital advertising. In early 2024, Google Mail users were automatically shown summaries of their emails via Gemini, Googleâ€™s AI assistantâ€”without opt-out options. This mirrors Googleâ€™s earlier rollout of AI Overviews in search results and Metaâ€™s mandatory deployment of Meta AI across Instagram, WhatsApp, and Messenger. These tools, while marketed as empowering personal assistants, operate without clear user consent and lack an â€œoffâ€ switch, prompting criticism from AI ethics researcher Sasha Luccioni, who noted users must navigate complex, unclear opt-out processes. Tech giants claim these AI agents enhance user experience by handling tasks like email drafting and travel planning. However, a Pew Research Center survey found most Americans want greater control over AI use. Google asserts AI-powered search increases user engagement and offers a â€œwebâ€ tab to filter AI results, though itâ€™s used in only a small fraction of searches. Meta claims users can choose to engage with Meta AI, but avoiding it is difficult, as itâ€™s embedded in core app functions like Instagram search. Behind the scenes, AI is fueling a new advertising economy. Companies like OpenAI now show ads in free ChatGPT versions based on user queries and browsing history. Google, while claiming no ads in Gemini, uses AI interactions to target ads on Google.com. The shift reflects a broader strategy: AI chatbots encourage users to voluntarily share intimate dataâ€”such as health interests or shopping habitsâ€”enabling hyper-personalized, often invasive, advertising. Experts like Madison and Wallâ€™s Luke Stillman liken this to â€œbad plastic surgeryâ€â€”subtle but pervasive. AI-driven personalization could also affect pricing. Googleâ€™s new AI shopping tool, developed with Shopify, Target, and Walmart, may enable dynamic pricing based on user data, such as budget or shopping behavior. Critics like Lindsay Owens of the Groundwork Collaborative warn this represents â€œsurveillance capitalism,â€ where personal data drives pricing disparitiesâ€”e.g., offering discounts to frugal users while charging more to those with higher budgets. Smaller firms like Mozilla and DuckDuckGo are pushing back. Firefox will soon offer granular AI controls, while DuckDuckGoâ€™s new search version filters AI-generated images, with 90% of users opting out. Yet, avoiding AI in Google and Metaâ€™s ecosystems remains nearly impossible. With 3.58 billion daily Meta users and Googleâ€™s 90% global search dominance, user loyalty persists despite dissatisfaction. As Kamyl Bazbaz of DuckDuckGo noted, â€œBig companies that have users locked in can get it wrong for a very long time before they ever get fired by a user.â€

    [Original] NLRB Dismisses Case Brought by Fired SpaceX Employees
    The National Labor Relations Board (N.L.R.B.) has dismissed a case accusing SpaceX of illegally firing eight employees who criticized CEO Elon Muskâ€™s social media conduct, citing lack of jurisdiction. In a Feb. 6 letter to the workersâ€™ attorneys, the agency stated that the National Mediation Board (NMB), which oversees airlines and railroads, has exclusive authority over the matter. SpaceX had argued it qualifies as a â€œcommon carrierâ€ due to its FAA licensing and public space travel bookings, a claim affirmed by the NMB in mid-January. The N.L.R.B. deferred to that decision, effectively ending the federal labor case. The dispute originated in 2022 when employees circulated a letter urging SpaceX to distance itself from Muskâ€™s dismissive remarks about sexual harassment allegations. Shortly after, several employees were fired. In 2024, the N.L.R.B. issued a complaint alleging the firings were retaliatory and violated employeesâ€™ rights to engage in protected collective activity. SpaceX countered that the N.L.R.B.â€™s structure violated constitutional separation of powersâ€”a claim previously dismissed by courtsâ€”and argued for NMB jurisdiction. Laurie Burgess, legal counsel for the fired workers, said the dismissal left their next steps uncertain, as the case now exists in uncharted legal territory. Matthew Bodie, a former N.L.R.B. attorney and law professor, noted that while SpaceXâ€™s argument has literal logic, the company operates unlike traditional common carriers. â€œSpaceX operates very differently than the airlines,â€ he said. â€œItâ€™s a stretch to call it a â€˜common carrier.â€™â€ The employees are pursuing separate harassment and retaliation claims in California courts. Critics have raised concerns about potential political influence, particularly given Muskâ€™s close ties to President Trump. During Muskâ€™s brief tenure leading the Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE), the N.L.R.B. faced staffing shortages due to unfilled vacancies under the Trump administration. Jennifer Abruzzo, former N.L.R.B. general counsel, accused the agency of losing its independence and prioritizing corporate interests, especially those of billionaire donors. In 2023, Muskâ€™s companiesâ€”Tesla and SpaceXâ€”secured $3 billion in contracts across 17 federal agencies. Around the time of Trumpâ€™s election, SpaceX faced at least 20 federal investigations, including the dismissed labor case. The caseâ€™s dismissal underscores broader concerns about regulatory capture and the erosion of worker protections.

    [Original] Ford Says Electric Vehicle Losses Will Continue for Three More Years
    A few years ago, Ford Motor jumped out ahead of other established automakers by quickly rolling out three electric vehicles that it hoped would help it sell more cars and increase profits. Instead, the company is paying a high price for its early start. On Tuesday, Ford said its electric vehicle division lost $4.8 billion in 2025 and was expected to lose $4 billion to $4.5 billion in 2026. The company also said that the division would continue losing money for at least two more years. â€œWe are now targeting break-even around 2029,â€ Fordâ€™s chief financial officer, Sherry House, said on Tuesday during a conference call to discuss the companyâ€™s financial results. Including the loss in 2025, Ford has lost more than $16 billion on its electric vehicle business since 2022. In December, Ford announced it was scaling back its electric vehicle plans. It stopped making one model, the F-150 Lightning pickup truck, scrapped plans to produce an electric truck at a plant it was building in Tennessee, and canceled plans for an electric commercial van. Instead, Ford plans to make a gas-electric hybrid version of the Lightning. The company will use the Tennessee factory to make a gasoline-powered truck, and will make hybrid and gas-powered delivery vans at a location in Ohio. Ford says it still planned to make a medium-size pickup that is supposed to sell for around $30,000. That truck, expected in 2027, will use new components and production methods that Ford has said will cost a lot less. It also ended a partnership with a Korean partner, SK On, that was supposed to jointly produce batteries. Ford has taken full ownership of a factory in Kentucky, and SK On now solely owns a plant in Tennessee. Ford took charges of $19.5 billion against its fourth quarter earnings to cover the cost of the changing its strategy. Overall, Ford lost $11.1 billion in the fourth quarter and $8.2 billion for all of 2025. The electric vehicle losses were offset by substantial profits in divisions that make internal-combustion vehicles and sell vehicles and services to commercial customers. Ford said it expected its financial performance to improve significantly in 2026. The company said this yearâ€™s adjusted earnings before interest, taxes and other items were expected to be $8 billion to $10 billion. In 2025, Ford said its adjusted earnings before interest, taxes and other items were $6.8 billion. Neal E. Boudette, a Michigan-based reporter for The Times, has been covering the auto industry for more than two decades. Share full articleRelated ContentAdvertisement

    [Original] These Mathematicians Are Putting A.I. to the Test
    A new study titled â€œFirst Proof,â€ led by Fields Medalist Martin Hairer and co-authored by mathematicians Mohammed Abouzaid, Lauren Williams, and Tamara Kolda, aims to objectively assess artificial intelligenceâ€™s ability to solve research-level mathematics. The project responds to growing concerns among students and researchers about AI rendering human mathematicians obsolete. Hairer, who won the 2014 Fields Medal and 2021 Breakthrough Prize, emphasized that while AI tools are useful, they have not yet demonstrated the capacity to generate genuinely new mathematical ideas. The team designed test questions drawn from their unpublished research, ensuring authenticity and relevance. These problems, encrypted and set to be released on February 13, were evaluated using OpenAIâ€™s ChatGPT-5.2 Pro and Googleâ€™s Gemini 3.0 Deep Think. Results showed that even top models struggled, often producing hand-wavy, inconsistent, or incorrect answersâ€”sometimes looping through revisions without convergence. One model answered a related but different question, while another ignored key problem details. Kolda noted the AIâ€™s confusion and revised the problem statement to improve clarity. Hairer observed that models excel at assembling known arguments but falter on critical reasoning, often over-explaining trivial parts while under-explaining core logic. The team views the project as a â€œfirst proofâ€ in the baking senseâ€”initial fermentation before a more structured second round. The paper was released on Euler Day (February 7), honoring Leonhard Euler, whose method underpins neural network training. The authors stress that while AI can assist with routine calculations, it lacks the creativity and depth required for true mathematical discovery. They caution against hype-driven discouragement of students and funders, advocating for independent, rigorous benchmarking. As Williams noted, mathematical research involves formulating big questions, designing frameworks, and solving sub-problemsâ€”only the third is currently measurable by AI. The team hopes the initiative will foster a more nuanced understanding of AIâ€™s role, not as a replacement, but as a tool requiring human oversight.

    [Original] Taiwan says proposal to move 40% of its chipmaking capacity to US is â€˜impossibleâ€™
    The new reality in geopolitics is the structural transformation from â€˜made-in-Taiwanâ€™ to â€˜made-by-Taiwanâ€™, according to one analyst Taiwanâ€™s move to defend its â€œsilicon shieldâ€ is the latest sign of the islandâ€™s tech dominance being used as a bargaining chip in trade negotiations, as it faces increased geopolitical pressure to shift semiconductor manufacturing capacity overseas, according to analysts. It would be â€œimpossibleâ€ to move 40 per cent of the islandâ€™s semiconductor capacity to the US, Taiwan officials have told the US, according to Taiwan vice-premier Cheng Li-chiun in an interview with local broadcaster Chinese Television System, which aired on Sunday. Chengâ€™s remarks signalled a willingness to hold onto Taiwanâ€™s most vital economic asset, as the US request could hollow out its prized semiconductor sector, comprising some of the worldâ€™s most advanced chipmakers such as Taiwan Semiconductor Manufacturing Co (TSMC), according to analysts. â€œForcing nearly 40 per cent of capacity to the US would trigger a severe risk of ecosystem disruptionâ€, said Arisa Liu, chief director and research fellow at Taiwan Industry Economics Services, a unit of the Taiwan Institute of Economic Research. It would not only cause production costs to increase exponentially due to the fragmentation of the supply chain, but also lead to low utilisation rates for expensive advanced manufacturing equipment due to the lack of mid- to high-level skilled workers in the US, Liu said. Chengâ€™s comments marked a pushback against recent statements by US Commerce Secretary Howard Lutnick, who called for a major production shift from Taiwan when the two sides reached a trade agreement last month.

    [Original] Tech war: Shanghai boosts chip fund 11-fold under Chinaâ€™s self-sufficiency drive
    Registered capital increases by US$794 million as countryâ€™s semiconductor hub strives to nurture local firms The Shanghai Integrated Circuit Industry Investment Fund, backed by the municipal government, has expanded one of its three funds more than 11-fold to pump more capital into the financial hubâ€™s chip firms as part of Chinaâ€™s broader pursuit of tech self-reliance. The third phase of the fund, also known as Shanghai IC Fund III, recently increased its registered capital by 5.5 billion yuan (US$794 million) to 6 billion yuan, according to business registry database Aiqicha. It added two new equity investors, namely Shanghai State-owned Capital Investment Leading IC Private Equity Investment Fund, which is set to inject 4.5 billion yuan, and Pudong Venture Capital, owned by the district government of Pudong, which is contributing 500 million yuan. The fund may grow even larger, given that the first and second phases, established in 2016 and 2020, respectively, each had registered capital of 24 billion yuan, Aiqicha data showed. The Shanghai IC Fund has invested in more than 20 local chip companies, including wafer foundries Semiconductor Manufacturing International Corp (SMIC) and HLMC, which is a subsidiary of Hua Hong Group, as well as ACM Research Shanghai, a semiconductor cleaning tool manufacturer. The fund is one in a series set up by local Chinese governments to strengthen their home-grown chip industries. The Beijing and Shenzhen governments also operate their own funds focused on long-term investments to address tough issues in the industry.

    [Original] Wrapped helps Spotify add users despite artists' criticism over fees
    ShareSaveFaarea MasudBusiness reporterShareSaveRick Polk/ Getty ImagesGlobal band KATSEYE attended Spotify's 2026 party celebrating new artists in Los AngelesMusic service Spotify has managed to boost the number of people streaming music, podcasts and audiobooks on the platform, despite increasing competition in the streaming industry. Paid subscribers in the last three months of 2025 jumped by 9 million, to 290 million - helping net profit rise to â‚¬1.17bn, the music giant said in its financial results released on Tuesday. Although the Swedish firm said it paid almost $11bn to artists, criticisms remain that the platform does not pay enough to musicians for having their songs on its platform. Spotify has over 750 million users, comprised of paying and non-paying subscribers, who each get a curated summary of their listening habits at the year-end. It highlighted its "Spotify Wrapped" feature for engaging users. "Our 11th annual Wrapped was bigger, bolder and more layered than ever, celebrating fans, artists, creators and authors around the world," it said in its results. "Wrapped had more than 300 million engaged users and more than 630 million shares on social media globally in 56 languages". Chief executive Gustav SÃ¶derstrÃ¶m said the firm considered itself the research and development department of the music industry, by focussing on new developments in audio, such as adding video to podcasts, and embracing music made by artificial intelligence (AI). "Our job is to understand new technologies quickly and capture their potential, which we've done time and again," he said. "The entire industry stands to benefit from this [AI] paradigm shift but we believe those who embrace this change and move fast, will benefit the most." But the latest revenue figures come as a heated debate continues about how much money artists and songwriters receive in royalties. Various artists boycotted a Spotify party in 2025, and Taylor Swift famously refused to put her work on the platform for three years because the platform didn't pay enough. The firm credited its expansion in users partly to audio e-books, though it did say: "The hard problems ahead â€“ in music, in podcasts, in books, in video, in live, and in things we haven't built yet â€“ we're going to keep building the technology to solve them." The band Massive Attack is the latest to boycott the firm, which it did in September 2025 saying Spotify was an "economic burden" on artists, and that fans' hard-earned money was fuelling its "lethal, dystopian technologies". The firm said it made $4.5b in total revenue in the final three months of 2025. Shares in the streaming jumped around 15% in trading following the financial results.

    [Original] Wegovy maker sues rival over 'knock-off' weight-loss drugs
    Danish pharmaceutical company Novo Nordisk has filed a lawsuit against Hims & Hers, accusing the US telehealth provider of selling unapproved, "unsafe, knock-off" versions of weight-loss drugs, including compounded pills and injections that infringe on Novo Nordiskâ€™s patents. The legal action, filed on Monday, seeks to ban Hims & Hersâ€™ weight-loss products, which the company claims are not authorized by the US Food and Drug Administration (FDA) and may contain dangerous impurities or incorrect dosages, potentially causing life-threatening immune responses. Novo Nordisk emphasized its intent to "protect public health and defend the scientific innovations that deliver better health outcomes to Americans." The dispute intensified after Hims & Hers launched a new weight-loss pill on Friday, prompting an initial threat from Novo Nordisk. The company responded over the weekend by halting sales of the product. On Monday, Hims & Hers criticized the lawsuit as a "blatant attack," accusing Novo Nordisk of "weaponizing the US judicial system to limit consumer choice," while its shares fell 16%. In contrast, Novo Nordiskâ€™s shares rose slightly on Tuesday. The conflict centers on compounding, a legal practice allowing US firms to produce customized medications not approved by the FDA, often for patients with specific needs. Hims & Hersâ€™ weight-loss products are compounded, unlike Novo Nordiskâ€™s FDA-approved Ozempic and Wegovy. The FDA announced on Friday it is taking steps to restrict the compounding of weight-loss drugs to "safeguard consumers from drugs for which the FDA cannot verify quality, safety, or efficacy," a move Novo Nordisk cited in its lawsuit. Kerry Fulford, a pharmaceutical analyst at Berenberg, described the lawsuit as Novo Nordiskâ€™s "first move" to clamp down on compounding, marking a strategic shift amid declining profits and patent expirations. The company has faced challenges recently, including thousands of job cuts in September and a warning to investors about a profit slump. Additionally, the FDA recently sent Novo Nordisk a letter criticizing a Wegovy advertisement for misleadingly implying benefits beyond weight loss, such as emotional relief or psychological improvement. Novo Nordisk stated it "takes all regulatory feedback seriously" and is responding to the FDAâ€™s concerns.

    [Original] Instagram and YouTube owners built 'addiction machines', trial hears
    A landmark California trial began in Los Angeles Superior Court, examining whether Instagram and YouTubeâ€™s platform designs caused mental health harm to a minor plaintiff, referred to as K.G.M. (Kaley G.M.), with attorneys for the plaintiff, Mark Lanier, accusing Meta and Google-owned YouTube of intentionally engineering addictive features to maximize user engagement. â€œThese companies built machines designed to addict the brains of children, and they did it on purpose,â€ Lanier declared, emphasizing internal documents and emails, including one from Meta CEO Mark Zuckerberg demanding a 12% increase in time spent on platforms. Lanier highlighted that YouTube targeted young users to charge advertisers more, calling the platform a â€œdigital babysitting serviceâ€ exploited by busy parents. He displayed childrenâ€™s blocks labeled â€œAddicting,â€ â€œBrains,â€ and â€œChildrenâ€ to underscore his argument that the companies engineered harm. In contrast, Metaâ€™s attorney Paul Schmidt argued that K.G.M.â€™s struggles stemmed from severe family trauma, including abuse, neglect, and bullying, citing records of therapy starting at age three and statements from K.G.M. describing her mother screaming at her and calling her â€œstupid,â€ which led her to contemplate suicide. Schmidt acknowledged the emotional weight of the testimony, stating, â€œIn a case thatâ€™s about psychological distress, that is what you have to consider.â€ The six-week trial, expected to feature testimony from Zuckerberg, Instagram head Adam Mosseri, YouTube CEO Neal Mohan, and former Meta whistleblowers, may set a precedent for thousands of similar cases. State attorneys general, including 29 in a separate federal case, have demanded an injunction requiring Meta to delete all under-13 accounts, erase data collected on minors, and disable addictive features like infinite scroll and autoplay. They also seek time restrictions for teens and the removal of beauty-enhancing filters, calling Metaâ€™s current teen account features â€œa public relations measure offering minimal real protections.â€ Snapchat and TikTok settled with K.G.M. last month and are no longer defendants. The trial unfolds as about 100 observers, including parents who believe their children died due to platform design, watched from the gallery. The companies maintain they are not liable for third-party content under federal law.

    [Original] Why food fraud persists, even with improving tech
    Food fraud, costing an estimated Â£81bn ($110bn) annually, remains largely unreported and difficult to quantify, with honey among the most commonly falsified foods due to its high value and widespread consumption. Fraudsters often substitute genuine honey with cheaper plant-based syrups like glucose from sugar cane, which can be half the price. Dr Juraj MajtÃ¡n of the Slovak Academy of Sciences emphasizes honeyâ€™s biological complexityâ€”containing hundreds of compounds from diverse sourcesâ€”making it hard to verify authenticity, especially without an internationally agreed definition. Even sophisticated fakes can mimic real honeyâ€™s taste, texture, and chemical profile, evading standard analysis. While methods like isotope and bond analysis exist, no single test can definitively confirm fraud, highlighting the urgent need for new detection tools. The primary harm lies in undermining beekeepersâ€™ livelihoods, though health risks exist, including allergens or toxins. Historical cases like the 2008 melamine-tainted infant formula scandal in China, which killed at least six babies, underscore the dangers. Dr Selvarani Elahi, UK deputy government chemist at LGC, warns that fraud persists despite severe consequences, citing ongoing risks in novel foods like insects, where mislabeling permitted species could trigger allergic reactions in shellfish-sensitive individuals. Fraud in spices remains a global issue, with industrial dyes like lead chromate added to paprika and cinnamonâ€”leading to hundreds of children being poisoned by lead-contaminated cinnamon in US applesauce in 2023. Though detection technology for dyes is robust, inconsistent regulatory surveillance undermines safety. Dr Karen Everstine of FoodChain ID notes rising labelling fraud, including false claims of extra virgin olive oil or organic status, with growing concerns over trendy superfoods and supplements fueled by social media hype. While advanced traceability tools like QR codes, microchips, and blockchain offer promise, they are limited by cost, counterfeiting risks, and impracticality for complex products like multi-ingredient meals. Elahi observes that blockchain has not solved food safety issues, especially for items with many global sources. Emerging technologiesâ€”thermal imaging, laser analysis, DNA profiling, and machine learningâ€”show potential for early risk detection, but speed and sensitivity remain challenges. Everstine stresses that rapid, field-ready testing is essential. Ultimately, low-tech solutions remain effective: buying from local beekeepers, as MajtÃ¡n advises, and heeding the rule of thumbâ€”â€œif it seems too good to be true, it probably is.â€ A $3 bottle of olive oil or honey in the US may be a red flag.

    [Original] Apple and Google agree to change app stores after 'effective duopoly' claim
    Apple and Google have agreed to modify their app store practices in the UK following intervention by the Competition and Markets Authority (CMA), which found the companies held an "effective duopoly" in the sector. The CMA, having granted both firms "strategic market status" in October 2025, demanded changes to promote competition and consumer choice. As part of the commitments, Apple and Google will no longer give preferential treatment to their own apps and will ensure transparency in third-party app approval processes. The CMA also secured pledges that neither company will misuse data collected from third-party developers in an unfair manner. CMA head Sarah Cardell stated the agreements represent "important first steps" and "will boost the UK's app economy," marking the first of many measures under the UKâ€™s digital markets competition regime. She emphasized the regimeâ€™s flexibility, enabling swift action on identified concerns. The UKâ€™s app economy, the largest in Europe, contributes an estimated 1.5% to GDP and supports around 400,000 jobs. Apple said it faces strong competition globally and remains committed to delivering high-quality products and user experiences. It described the new commitments as reflecting its "constructive engagement" with the CMA and a "pragmatic approach to regulation." Google acknowledged its Play Store practices are fair and transparent but welcomed the opportunity to resolve CMA concerns collaboratively. Technology analyst Paolo Pescatore called the move a "pragmatic first step," though some may view it as addressing only "low-hanging fruit." He cautioned that further, more stringent measures are likely, noting the developments are not the final outcome. The CMA will closely monitor implementation and may enforce formal changes if commitments are not upheld. The UKâ€™s digital markets regime, inspired by but distinct from the EUâ€™s Digital Markets Act, targets "gatekeeper" platforms to ensure fair competition. For example, Apple has previously been required to allow alternative web browsers to be displayed alongside Safari. Apple has argued that interoperability mandates could compromise privacy and security. The CMAâ€™s actions underscore its ongoing efforts to balance innovation with fair market access in the UKâ€™s digital landscape.

    [Original] More solar farms on the way after record renewables auction
    The UK government has awarded contracts to a record 157 solar projects across England, Scotland, and Wales, adding 4.9GW of capacityâ€”up from 3.3GW in the 2024 auctionâ€”marking a significant step toward its 2030 clean energy target. The contracts, part of a broader renewables push, also include 1.3GW of onshore wind projects, primarily in Scotland, and a small number of tidal power developments. Solar projects will receive a fixed price of Â£65/MWh (2024 prices), down from Â£70/MWh in 2024, while onshore wind prices rose slightly to Â£72/MWh. These long-term, inflation-linked contracts aim to secure developer investment. The government aims for 45â€“47GW of solar capacity by 2030, potentially rising to 54â€“57GW with rooftop solar, up from 21GW as of autumn 2025 (industry estimates place current capacity at 24GW). Solar contributed over 6% of UK electricity last year, peaking at over 40% in July. The West Burton solar farm, on the Lincolnshire-Nottinghamshire border, is the largest to secure a contract, sparking local opposition over concerns about "mass industrialisation" of the countryside. While climate groups welcome the move as a cost-effective way to reduce fossil fuel relianceâ€”particularly in summerâ€”analysts remain sceptical about meeting the 2030 goal due to grid connection challenges. Energy Secretary Ed Miliband hailed the move as a way to "drive bills down" and reduce dependence on volatile gas markets, while shadow energy secretary Claire Coutinho warned of rising costs from grid upgrades and backup needs. The SNP supports renewables and calls for Scottish energy autonomy, while Plaid Cymru opposes large solar farms on farmland. Reform UK questions the net zero agenda, and the Lib Dems and Greens advocate for expanded renewables to combat climate change and create green jobs. Tidal projects, though costly, are seen as future investments. The government also launched its "Local Power Plan," pledging up to Â£1bnâ€”part of funds for state-owned Great British Energyâ€”for community-owned energy projects, including solar on public buildings.

    [Original] US to exempt some Bangladeshi clothes from tariffs
    ShareSaveOsmond ChiaBusiness reporterShareSaveGetty ImagesBangladesh is a major producer of clothesBangladesh has secured exemptions for some clothes and textiles that are made with US-produced materials, as part of a new agreement announced on Monday. As part of the deal, Washington will also cut its tariffs on Bangladesh from 20% to 19%, in exchange for Dhaka to open its markets to a wider range of American goods. The apparel industry forms the backbone of Bangladesh, which is the world's second largest exporter of clothes after China. The South Asian country has been in long-drawn talks with the White House after President Donald Trump imposed sweeping tariffs on global trading partners in April last year. The White House said in a joint statement between the sides that the agreement will strengthen the countries' economic ties and offer both "unprecedented access" to each market. It said the US will lower its tariff rate on Bangladesh and will also identify certain clothing and textile goods from the country to enter the US free of tariffs. The goods include those produced with American cotton and man-made textiles, the statement said. The volume of these will be determined by how much textiles the US exports to Bangladesh. The clothing sector accounts for more than 80% of Bangladesh's total export revenue and employs around four million workers. In exchange, Bangladesh has agreed to provide "significant preferential market access" to a host of American agricultural and industrial goods. These include opening up its markets to more US chemicals, medical devices, car parts, soy products and meat, said the White House. The BBC has contacted the Bangladeshi government for comment. As part of the agreement announced on Monday, Dhaka will recognise American food and drug and vehicle safety and emission rules, making it easier for US goods to enter the country. Bangladesh also committed to observe internationally recognised labour rights, ramp up its environmental protection efforts, and uphold its agreement to buy billions of dollars of American agriculture, aircraft and energy products, according to the statement. Bangladesh is set to head to the polls on Thursday for general elections. The country has been led by an interim government since 2024, when former Prime Minister Sheikh Hasina fled to India after being ousted over the fatal crackdown on student-led protests. The US's newly announced tariff cut puts Bangladesh nearly level with its neighbour and regional competitor India, which faces an 18% levy from the US. Both South Asian countries compete to export clothes, footwear, along with agricultural goods. India was initially hit with 25% US levies when Trump announced his first round of reciprocal tariffs in April 2025. Bangladesh, on the other hand, was given a 37% tariff.

    [Original] Japan has given Takaichi a landslide win - but can she bring back the economy?
    Japanâ€™s Prime Minister Sanae Takaichi has secured a decisive victory in a snap election, winning 316 of 465 seats in the Diet, marking one of the strongest mandates in recent decades. Takaichi, who campaigned on tax cuts and increased public investment to stimulate growth, is now tasked with tackling Japanâ€™s entrenched challengesâ€”sluggish growth, the worldâ€™s highest public debt, and a shrinking, ageing population. He urges the Bank of Japan to continue raising interest rates and calls for tighter fiscal policy to attract foreign investment and stabilize the yen. A weaker yen boosts exports but raises import costs and makes living abroad more expensive, while also fueling tourism-driven inflation and backlash in some areas. Japanâ€™s workforce is shrinking, with acute shortages in construction, care, agriculture, and hospitality. Though foreign worker numbers have risen slightly due to relaxed rules, immigration remains politically sensitive, and Takaichi shows little inclination to expand it. Japanâ€™s economic future hinges on innovation and reform, yet resistance to change has hindered progress. Success will require navigating delicate trade-offs between fiscal expansion, inflation control, and geopolitical realignment.

    [Original] NLRB Dismisses Case Brought by Fired SpaceX Employees
    The National Labor Relations Board (N.L.R.B.) has dismissed a case accusing SpaceX of illegally firing eight employees who criticized CEO Elon Muskâ€™s social media conduct, citing lack of jurisdiction. In a Feb. 6 letter to the workersâ€™ lawyers, the N.L.R.B. stated that the National Mediation Board (N.M.B.), which oversees airlines and railroads, has exclusive authority over the matter. SpaceX had argued that it qualifies as a â€œcommon carrierâ€ due to its FAA license and public space travel booking access, a claim affirmed by the N.M.B. in mid-January. The N.L.R.B. has now deferred to that decision, effectively ending the federal labor case. The dispute originated in 2022 when employees circulated a letter urging SpaceX to distance itself from Muskâ€™s dismissive remarks about sexual harassment allegations. Several were fired shortly after. In 2024, the N.L.R.B. issued a complaint, asserting the firings were retaliatory and violated employeesâ€™ federally protected rights to engage in collective activity. SpaceX challenged the complaint on constitutional grounds, arguing the N.L.R.B.â€™s structure violates separation of powersâ€”a claim courts have previously rejected. However, the recent dismissal hinges on jurisdiction, not constitutionality. Laurie Burgess, legal counsel for the fired workers, said the next steps are unclear, as the case now exists in uncharted legal territory. Matthew Bodie, a former N.L.R.B. attorney and law professor, noted that while SpaceXâ€™s argument has literal logic, the company operates more like a private contractor than a common carrier, as space travel access remains highly restricted. â€œItâ€™s a stretch to call it a â€˜common carrier,â€™â€ he said. The employees continue pursuing separate harassment and retaliation claims in California courts. Critics have raised concerns about potential political influence, particularly given Muskâ€™s close ties to President Trump. During Muskâ€™s brief tenure leading the Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE), the N.L.R.B. faced staffing vacancies and operational challenges. Jennifer Abruzzo, former N.L.R.B. general counsel, accused the agency of losing its independence and prioritizing corporate interests, especially those of billionaire donors. In 2023, Muskâ€™s companiesâ€”Tesla and SpaceXâ€”secured $3 billion in contracts across 17 federal agencies. Around the time of Trumpâ€™s election, SpaceX faced at least 20 federal investigations, including the original labor case. The dismissal has sparked broader concerns about regulatory capture and the erosion of worker protections.

    [Original] Laegreid wins bronze then confesses to affair on TV
    Norwegian biathlete Sturla Holm Laegreid, a seven-time world champion, won bronze in the 20km individual biathlon at the Milan-Cortina Winter Olympics, finishing behind gold medalist Johan-Olav Botn and silver medalist Eric Perrot of France.     [Original] Pilot praised after crash-landing faulty Somali passenger plane on seashore
    ShareSaveAbdinasir AliBBC SomaliShareSaveWatch: Passenger plane in shallow water after it failed to stop on the runwayAn airline in Somalia has praised one of its pilots after he crash-landed his passenger plane, which had suffered a technical fault, on the shoreline next to the capital's international airport with all 55 on board surviving. Starsky Aviation said the pilot's quick thinking was crucial in saving the 50 passengers and five crew. The crew of the aircraft, a Fokker 50, reported a problem shortly after take off from Mogadishu on Tuesday morning and requested that the plane return, Somalia's Civil Aviation Authority (CAA) said. It then touched down but failed to stop on the runway, overshooting the tarmac before coming to rest in shallow water, the CAA's director Ahmed Macalin Hassan said. It is not clear yet exactly what the issue was. Footage posted on X appeared to show passengers leaving the aircraft and walking away from the wreckage on the shore of the Indian Ocean. No serious injuries have been reported. The African Union's mission in Somalia said UN and AU troops were "swiftly deployed" to help with rescue efforts. Somalia's transport minister was also at the scene, its post on X added. "We are relieved to confirm that all passengers and crew are safe. Investigations are under way to establish what caused the technical issue that led to the emergency landing," Starsky spokesman Hassan Mohamed Aden said. "The pilot's swift and calm decision-making played a decisive role in ensuring the safety of everyone on board, and we commend him for how he handled the situation," he added. Mogadishu's international airport is right next to the Indian OceanGetty Images/BBCGo to BBCAfrica.com for more news from the African continent.     [Original] Bid launched to extend Zimbabwe president's term in office
    Zimbabweâ€™s cabinet has approved draft legislation that would allow President Emmerson Mnangagwa, 83, to extend his tenure until at least 2030. Under the proposed changes, presidents would be elected by parliament rather than through direct popular vote, with a maximum of two seven-year termsâ€”up from the current five-year limit. Justice Minister Ziyambi Ziyambi confirmed public consultations would precede parliamentary debate, where both chambers are dominated by the ruling Zanu-PF party. Constitutional experts warn that altering term limits requires a referendum and argue such amendments cannot benefit a sitting president. Mnangagwa, who seized power in 2017 after a military coup ousted Robert Mugabe, won re-election in 2018 and again in 2023, though both results were disputed. Known as â€œthe crocodileâ€ for his political acumen, his current term ends in 2028. The push to extend his rule began two years ago, with supporters chanting â€œ2030 he will still be the leaderâ€ at Zanu-PF rallies, referencing his â€œAgenda 2030â€ development programmeâ€”though Mnangagwa has publicly rejected the idea. His main internal critic, Blessed Geza, known as â€œBombshell,â€ died last week in South Africa. Geza, a veteran of the 1970s liberation war and former central committee member, had accused Mnangagwa of nepotism and disloyalty, apologizing for helping him rise to power. Expelled from Zanu-PF, Geza continued to rally opposition via social media, urging protests against corruption and the â€œplunder of our country.â€ His final post called for a â€œnoble warâ€ to remove Mnangagwa. Andrease Ethan Mathibela, national chairman of the Zimbabwe National Liberation War Veterans Association, praised Geza for choosing to speak out despite risks. The government maintains the draft law aims to strengthen governance and ensure political stability. The bill now moves toward parliamentary review, with legal challenges expected.

    [Original] French former teacher charged with abusing 89 teens dating back to 1960s
    Jacques Leveugle, 79, has been charged with the rape and sexual assault of 89 teenagers in a case spanning from 1967 to 2022, with allegations extending across France, Germany, Switzerland, Morocco, Niger, Algeria, the Philippines, India, Colombia, and New Caledonia. His nephew, suspecting misconduct, examined a USB drive during October 2023 and discovered â€œ15 tomes of very dense materialâ€ â€” photographs and written accounts detailing alleged sexual relations with minors aged 13 to 17. He described Leveugle as having a â€œcomplex personality,â€ noting that victims reported he often helped them learn foreign languages and culture. Authorities are still working to identify victims whose names appear only by first name in the journal.     [Original] Chappell Roan leaves talent agency led by Casey Wasserman after Epstein fallout
    ShareSaveTabby WilsonShareSaveGetty ImagesSinger Chappell Roan says she has left the talent agency led by Casey Wasserman, whose name appears in the Epstein files. Announcing her split with the agency, Roan said she has a "duty to protect her team" and her decision reflected her belief that "meaningful change in our industry requires accountability". Wasserman has been criticised after his flirtatious emails to Ghislaine Maxwell, sent in 2003, were revealed among the millions of files published in relation to convicted paedophile Jeffrey Epstein. Roan made no mention of Epstein, nor the Epstein files, in her statement on Instagram announcing her departure. "As of today, I am no longer represented by Wasserman, the talent agency led by Casey Wasserman," she said. Roan added: "No artist, agent or employee should ever be expected to defend or overlook actions that conflict so deeply with our own moral values." The BBC has reached out to Wasserman for comment. Wasserman is also the chairman of the Los Angeles 2028 Olympic Games, and has faced calls to step down from the position following the release of the emails. He has said he "deeply regrets" the messages exchanged with Maxwell, who is currently serving a 20-year prison sentence for recruiting and trafficking teenage girls to be sexually abused by Epstein. He said in a statement that his correspondence with Maxwell "took place over two decades ago, long before her horrific crimes came to light". Wasserman also emphasised that he had "never had a personal or business relationship with Jeffrey Epstein". "As is well documented, I went on a humanitarian trip as part of a delegation with the Clinton Foundation in 2002 on the Epstein plane," he said. "I am terribly sorry for having any association with either of them." Wasserman has not been accused of wrongdoing by any of Epstein's victims, and the appearance of his name in the files does not imply criminal activity of any kind. Roan's announcement comes after two other bands represented by Wasserman released statements indicating they wanted to distance themselves from his agency. Wednesday, a self-described indie rock band, said they were "aghast" to see Wasserman feature in the Epstein files and did not want to continue to be associated with him. They said that they hoped he would step down "for the sake of his staff". Rock band Beach Bunny said they were "hugely disappointed and disgusted" that Wasserman "had involvement with Ghislaine Maxwell".

    [Original] Marc Anthony says the way Beckham feud has played out is 'hardly the truth'
    ShareSaveSteven McIntoshEntertainment reporterShareSaveGetty ImagesSinger Marc Anthony has described the Beckham family rift as "extremely unfortunate", but added that the way it has played out is "hardly the truth". The 57-year-old performed at Brooklyn and Nicola Peltz Beckham's wedding reception in 2022, and is a close friend of the wider family. But Brooklyn recently said the way the couple's first dance was handled at the wedding left him feeling "uncomfortable and humiliated", after Anthony reportedly called for him to dance with his mother instead of his wife. Beckham added that his mother then danced "very inappropriately" on him. Sir David and Lady Beckham have not commented since Brooklyn published his statement. Speaking to the Hollywood Reporter, Anthony said: "I have nothing to say about what's happening with the family. They're a wonderful, wonderful family. "I've known them since before the kids were born. I'm godfather to Cruz. I'm really close to the family. But I have nothing to say about what happened there." He added: "It's extremely unfortunate how it's playing out - but [how it's playing out] is hardly the truth." Brooklyn Beckham published a six-page Instagram statement on 19 January, confirming a rift between him and his wife with the wider Beckham family. He accused his parents of trying to "ruin my relationship" with Peltz, adding that he had no wish to reconcile with his family. The 26-year-old also said his mother had "hijacked" his first dance with Peltz, which had been "planned weeks in advance to a romantic love song". "In front of our 500 wedding guests," he continued, "Marc Anthony called me to the stage, where in the schedule was planned to be my romantic dance with my wife but instead my mum was waiting to dance with me instead." "She danced very inappropriately on me in front of everyone. I've never felt more uncomfortable or humiliated in my entire life." Wedding DJ Fat Tony previously told ITV's This Morning that "the whole situation was really awkward for everyone in the room". After speculation about the nature of Lady Beckham's dancing, Fat Tony clarified: "There was no slut-dropping, there was no black cat PVC catsuits, there was no Spice Girl action." Fat Tony claimed Marc Anthony had called for "the most beautiful woman in the room" to come up for the first dance with Brooklyn, but then said Lady Beckham's name instead of Nicola's. The DJ said this led to the bride running out of the room in tears. Sir David and Lady Beckham have not responded to repeated requests for comment on the claims in their eldest son's statement However, when asked about young people and their social media use in Davos last month, Sir David remarked that children are "allowed to make mistakes".
